Now for the harvest

## Quick Walkthrough

- Speak with [Esbern](/wiki/Skyrim:Esbern "Skyrim:Esbern").
- Acquire a [dragon bone](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Bone "Skyrim:Dragon Bone") and a [dragon scale](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Scales "Skyrim:Dragon Scales").
- Return to Esbern.
- Drink the [potion](/wiki/Skyrim:Esbern%27s_Potion "Skyrim:Esbern's Potion").
- Speak with Esbern once more to complete the quest.

## Detailed Walkthrough

Once you have three followers recruited as [Blades](/wiki/Skyrim:Blades "Skyrim:Blades"), you can ask [Esbern](/wiki/Skyrim:Esbern "Skyrim:Esbern") for [dragons](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon "Skyrim:Dragon") to kill. Once you agree to kill one, Esbern will send you to a random place where you'll find a dragon. After you kill the dragon, you'll get the update to the quest stating "Return to Esbern". Return and speak to him; he'll ask for a [dragon bone](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Bone "Skyrim:Dragon Bone") and a [dragon scale](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Scales "Skyrim:Dragon Scales"). Give him the dragon bone and scale and he'll give you a [potion](/wiki/Skyrim:Esbern%27s_Potion "Skyrim:Esbern's Potion"). Drink the potion to gain the [Dragon Infusion](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Infusion "Skyrim:Dragon Infusion") perk. Speak with him once more to complete the quest. The potion adds the permanent perk of 25% less melee damage from dragons.

## Bugs

- You do not gain the perk after drinking the potion and it is not obtainable via normal gameplay means.
  - The [Official Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim:Patch "Skyrim:Patch"), version 1.9, fixes this bug.
- The quest journal entry won't update after quest completion.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 1.0, fixes this bug.
  -  If you don't want an uncompleted quest stuck in their quest log, you have the opportunity to back out of dialogue with Esbern after the 'Talk to Esbern' objective but before you inquire about a dragon location. Note: This bug does not appear to be present in the Anniversary Edition.[*verification needed — how is this affected by the [Paarthurnax](/wiki/Skyrim:Paarthurnax_(quest) "Skyrim:Paarthurnax (quest)") quest?*]
  -  **Workaround** - Basically, you must *not* give the dragon's bone and scale to Esbern; use console commands instead. There are three contexts to consider, each with its own solution: the first one is before returning to Esbern, the second one is before turning-in the dragon's scale and bone asked by Esbern, and the third one is after getting the potion (after giving the dragon's scale and bone).
    - **Before returning to Esbern** - You killed the dragon and got a new journal entry stating "Return to Esbern". Use the console to add the perk : `player.addspell 000F5FFA`. From then on, you won't be asked to retrieve a dragon's scale and bones and thus won't receive the resulting potion (it seems that one condition for triggering the quest is set by detecting that you don't have the perk yet).
    - **Before turning-in a dragon's scale and bone (recommended)** - You've returned to Esbern and told him that the dragon is dead, which triggered a new quest requiring a dragon's bone and scale. In the console, type:

      :   ```
          player.addspell 000F5FFA
          SetObjectiveCompleted FreeFormSkyHavenTempleD 10 1
          ```
    - **After giving bone and scale to Esbern** - The quest has already been started and it's supposed to be completed, but the journal entry is still there : you've given the dragon's bone and scale and thus received the potion, however without any effect after you drank it since it has a bug (no perk imbued). You must first reset the quest so as to start it over again, then add the perk to your powers, and finally clear the entry from your journal with the quest set as "completed". In the console, type:

      :   ```
          ResetQuest FreeFormSkyHavenTempleD
          SetStage FreeFormSkyHavenTempleD 10
          player.addspell 000F5FFA
          SetObjectiveCompleted FreeFormSkyHavenTempleD 10 1
          ```
    - **How to fix/finish this quest?** - Set quest as "completed". In the console, type:

      :   ```
          SetStage FreeFormSkyHavenTempleD 100
          ```
- You can get Esbern's Potion quest line without recruiting any Blades. However, it will not be titled "Dragon Research" and is located in Miscellaneous Quests. After completing Alduin's Wall (also may happen before you even visit Esbern), killing a dragon at a defined radiant location (such as a word wall) will trigger the objective "Return to Esbern". Speaking to Esbern then triggers "Give a Dragon Scale and a Dragon Bone to Esbern". When you give them to him, he will give you Esbern's Potion.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 1.2.5, fixes this bug.

## Quest Stages

| Dragon Research (FreeformSkyHavenTempleD) | | |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Stage | Finishes Quest | Journal Entry |
| 10 |  | *Objective 10:* Bring a Dragon Scale and a Dragon Bone to Esbern |

- The following empty quest stages were omitted from the table: 100.

Notes

- Any text displayed in angle brackets (e.g., `<Alias=LocationHold>`) is dynamically set by the Radiant Quest system, and will be filled in with the appropriate word(s) when seen in game.
- Not all Journal Entries may appear in your journal; which entries appear and which entries do not depends on the manner in which the quest is done.
- Stages are not always in order of progress. This is usually the case with quests that have multiple possible outcomes or quests where certain tasks may be done in any order. Some stages may therefore repeat objectives seen in other stages.
- If an entry is marked as "Finishes Quest" it means the quest disappears from the Active Quest list, but you may still receive new entries for that quest.
- On the PC, it is possible to use the [console](/wiki/Skyrim:Console "Skyrim:Console") to advance through the quest by entering `setstage FreeformSkyHavenTempleD stage`, where `stage` is the number of the stage you wish to complete. It is not possible to un-complete (i.e. go back) quest stages, but it is possible to clear all stages of the quest using `resetquest FreeformSkyHavenTempleD`.

# Skyrim:Dragon Rising

## Overview

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| [SR-qico-Main.png](/wiki/File:SR-qico-Main.png) | **Investigate a [dragon](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon "Skyrim:Dragon") sighting near [Whiterun](/wiki/Skyrim:Whiterun "Skyrim:Whiterun").** |

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| Quest Giver: | [Farengar Secret-Fire](/wiki/Skyrim:Farengar_Secret-Fire "Skyrim:Farengar Secret-Fire") |
| Location(s): | [Dragonsreach](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragonsreach "Skyrim:Dragonsreach"), The [Western Watchtower](/wiki/Skyrim:Western_Watchtower "Skyrim:Western Watchtower") outside Whiterun |
| Reward: | Ability to use Dragon Shouts, Axe of Whiterun, [Thaneship](/wiki/Skyrim:Thane "Skyrim:Thane") of Whiterun, [Lydia](/wiki/Skyrim:Lydia "Skyrim:Lydia") as a follower |
| [Disposition](/wiki/Skyrim:Disposition "Skyrim:Disposition"): | =3 (Balgruuf) |
| ID: | MQ104 |
| --- | |
| |  |  | | --- | --- | | **← Previous** [Bleak Falls Barrow](/wiki/Skyrim:Bleak_Falls_Barrow_(quest) "Skyrim:Bleak Falls Barrow (quest)") | **Next →** [The Way of the Voice](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Way_of_the_Voice "Skyrim:The Way of the Voice") [The Whispering Door](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Whispering_Door "Skyrim:The Whispering Door") [In My Time Of Need](/wiki/Skyrim:In_My_Time_Of_Need "Skyrim:In My Time Of Need") | | |
| |  |  | | --- | --- | | ← Previous | [Bleak Falls Barrow](/wiki/Skyrim:Bleak_Falls_Barrow_(quest) "Skyrim:Bleak Falls Barrow (quest)") | | → Next | [The Way of the Voice](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Way_of_the_Voice "Skyrim:The Way of the Voice") [The Whispering Door](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Whispering_Door "Skyrim:The Whispering Door") [In My Time Of Need](/wiki/Skyrim:In_My_Time_Of_Need "Skyrim:In My Time Of Need") | | |

Dragon attack at the Western Watchtower!

## Quick Walkthrough

1. Talk to [Jarl Balgruuf](/wiki/Skyrim:Balgruuf_the_Greater "Skyrim:Balgruuf the Greater").
2. Meet [Irileth](/wiki/Skyrim:Irileth "Skyrim:Irileth") near the [Western Watchtower](/wiki/Skyrim:Western_Watchtower "Skyrim:Western Watchtower").
3. Kill [Mirmulnir](/wiki/Skyrim:Mirmulnir "Skyrim:Mirmulnir"), a dragon.
4. (Optional) Use your new Shout power.
5. Report back to Jarl Balgruuf.

## Detailed Walkthrough

Irileth rallying the guards

### Talk to Jarl Balgruuf

Shortly after you return the Dragonstone to [Farengar](/wiki/Skyrim:Farengar_Secret-Fire "Skyrim:Farengar Secret-Fire"), Irileth will approach to inform him that there has been a sighting of a dragon at Whiterun's [Western Watchtower](/wiki/Skyrim:Western_Watchtower "Skyrim:Western Watchtower") not far west of the city. Irileth will then ask Farengar and you to meet with Jarl Balgruuf. Follow them there, where a somewhat unnerved [Whiterun guard](/wiki/Skyrim:Whiterun_Guard "Skyrim:Whiterun Guard") will recount seeing a [dragon](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon "Skyrim:Dragon") flying over the watchtower. Balgruuf will ask you to accompany [Irileth](/wiki/Skyrim:Irileth "Skyrim:Irileth"), as she goes to investigate and, if necessary, do battle. She will recruit several Whiterun Guards along the way.

### Meet Irileth near the Western Watchtower

*"No! Get back! It's still here somewhere! Hroki and Tor just got grabbed when they tried to make a run for it!"*

Follow Irileth to the [Guard Barracks](/wiki/Skyrim:Guard_Barracks_(Gate) "Skyrim:Guard Barracks (Gate)") just inside the city gates. After she delivers a speech to rally her soldiers, follow them west towards the tower.

You will gather near the road close to the watchtower to find the watchtower burned and smoking, evidently signs of a recent attack by a dragon. After a short talk, Irileth will give orders to search for survivors. On the north side of the tower, on or around the ramp leading to the interior, you will encounter the lone surviving Whiterun Guard, stammering about what he's just experienced. Shortly after hearing this, you will hear several warnings that the dragon has returned. Irileth will advise taking cover against the dragon's attacks and to *"make every arrow count"*.

### Kill the Dragon

The dragon, [Mirmulnir](/wiki/Skyrim:Mirmulnir "Skyrim:Mirmulnir"), will approach from the south and will immediately begin attacking the group. Use [dragon combat strategies](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon "Skyrim:Dragon") during the battle. He will land, fight, and then fly off after losing about a quarter of his health. Once further wounded, he will remain on the ground. While at a level of around 20 or lower, Mirmulnir will be a dragon that uses fire attacks, is resistant to [fire damage](/wiki/Skyrim:Fire_Damage "Skyrim:Fire Damage"), and is weak against [frost damage](/wiki/Skyrim:Frost_Damage "Skyrim:Frost Damage"). Ranged weapons, frost or shock attacks, and melee weapons will be effective choices. If you play this quest at higher levels, Mirmulnir may attack with [frost](/wiki/Skyrim:Frost_Breath "Skyrim:Frost Breath").

When in the air, the dragon will use [shouts](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Shouts "Skyrim:Dragon Shouts"), typically [Fire Breath](/wiki/Skyrim:Fire_Breath "Skyrim:Fire Breath"), against you, the others, and any other living creature who may happen to be in the area. Dragons are indiscriminate in their attacks, so the presence of multiple targets should relieve you of some of the onslaught. He may also use the somewhat more powerful [Fireball](/wiki/Skyrim:Fireball "Skyrim:Fireball") shout. When his attention is focused elsewhere, attack with a ranged weapon or spell. If he begins to aim his face toward you while in the air, seek cover to shield you against the powerful shout that will ensue. If you get inside the watchtower, or near its door, you can effectively use its walls for this, and then step back out, or use a window or doorway to counter-attack when his shout has dissipated.

When on the ground, Mirmulnir uses both physical and magic attacks. If facing you from a moderate distance, he will use his Thu'um (shouts) against you, as long as you are in his line of sight. When up-close, he will attack frontally with his jaws. If you are behind him, he will beat his tail on the ground, trying to hit you. Both of these types of attacks deal heavy physical damage.

Mirmulnir approaches

The dragon's wing attacks, while very strong, are the least powerful of his physical attacks. When the dragon is in the air, attack at every safe opportunity until he is forced to land. When he's on the ground, the best approach is from the side. Irileth is also useful in this fight. As an [essential character](/wiki/Skyrim:Essential_NPCs "Skyrim:Essential NPCs") in the game, she can be weakened but not killed in the attacks.

Once killed, Mirmulnir will explode in flames, and then release his soul in a blast of energy. As the [Dovahkiin](/wiki/Skyrim:Dovahkiin "Skyrim:Dovahkiin") (or "Dragonborn"), the dragon's soul will enter your body, automatically unlocking the first word of the [Unrelenting Force](/wiki/Skyrim:Unrelenting_Force "Skyrim:Unrelenting Force") shout, which you learned previously during the [Bleak Falls Barrow quest](/wiki/Skyrim:Bleak_Falls_Barrow_(quest) "Skyrim:Bleak Falls Barrow (quest)").

After witnessing you consume the dragon's soul, a nearby guard will engage you in dialogue and exclaim that you are Dragonborn. Some of the other surviving guards will express their skepticism. Irileth will discard the notion as a myth and order you to report back to the jarl. One guard will remark that if you are Dragonborn, you can shout, and ask if you've tried. You can use your shout at this time, completing the optional quest objective, or leave them wondering.

Search the dragon's body, taking [dragon bones](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Bone "Skyrim:Dragon Bone") and [dragon scales](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Scales "Skyrim:Dragon Scales") along with other loot. These can be used to forge and improve [dragonbone and dragonscale armor and weapons](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Armor "Skyrim:Dragon Armor")[DG](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard "Skyrim:Dawnguard") once your [Smithing skills](/wiki/Skyrim:Smithing "Skyrim:Smithing") are highly advanced. In the lengthy intervening period, you can sell these valuable items. Search in and around the tower for any loot you can take from dead guards.

### Report Back to Jarl Balgruuf

As you make your way back to Whiterun (note that the Dragonsreach marker will vanish temporarily during this quest), you should hear thundering voices boom out *"DOVAHKIIN!"*, reverberate across the sky. Return to Dragonsreach and report to Jarl Balgruuf.

He will ask you to recount events at the watchtower and then conclude that the voices were the [Greybeards](/wiki/Skyrim:Greybeards "Skyrim:Greybeards"), *"masters of the way of the Voice"*, summoning you to their secluded mountain peak residence at [High Hrothgar](/wiki/Skyrim:High_Hrothgar "Skyrim:High Hrothgar"). The jarl will inform you that the greybeards can teach you to use your gift. The jarl advises you to travel to the Greybeards immediately, as their summons is a *"great honor"*.

During your exchange with the jarl, his brother Hrongar will counsel confidence in you as the Dragonborn, in a calm debate with [Proventus Avenicci](/wiki/Skyrim:Proventus_Avenicci "Skyrim:Proventus Avenicci"), the jarl's [Steward](/wiki/Skyrim:Steward "Skyrim:Steward"), who openly expresses suspicion and skepticism toward you.

For your assistance in slaying the dragon, the jarl will appoint you [Thane](/wiki/Skyrim:Thane "Skyrim:Thane") of Whiterun, which entitles you to a personal [housecarl](/wiki/Skyrim:Housecarl "Skyrim:Housecarl"), [Lydia](/wiki/Skyrim:Lydia "Skyrim:Lydia"). She will reside at Dragonsreach until you purchase [Breezehome](/wiki/Skyrim:Breezehome "Skyrim:Breezehome"), at which point she will move in with you. Balgruuf will also reward you with the Axe of Whiterun as your symbol of office. The axe is a leveled weapon that carries a random [enchantment effect](/wiki/Skyrim:Enchantments#Weapon_Effects "Skyrim:Enchantments").

Lydia will greet you if you head toward the front door of Dragonsreach, at which point you can make her a [follower](/wiki/Skyrim:Followers "Skyrim:Followers") by telling her that you need her help.

### Achievement

After Mirmulnir is killed, you will earn:

-  **Dragon Soul** (10 points/Bronze) — Absorb a [dragon](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon "Skyrim:Dragon") soul

## Notes

- This quest was originally tied to the [civil war](/wiki/Skyrim:Civil_War "Skyrim:Civil War"), and would've had two versions, similar to [The Jagged Crown](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Jagged_Crown "Skyrim:The Jagged Crown"). That quest was originally known internally as `MQ103`, and still has a lot of leftovers related to this earlier placement. The main differences being that it was to part of the Main Questline (MQ) instead of the Civil War quests (CW), and that it would've been the prerequisite to unlocking dragon spawns, as this quest would've followed it, as it stayed `MQ104`. `MQ104A` would've been the Legion version, with `MQ104B` being the Stormcloak version. Both versions have numerous leftovers still in the files, and the finalized quest reuses markers, AI packages, and dialogue from both. The Stormcloak version would've seen you investigate reports of a dragon attack on [Fort Amol](/wiki/Skyrim:Fort_Amol "Skyrim:Fort Amol") alongside an NPC referred to only as "Sifnar", while the Legion version would've seen you travel with [Captain Metilius](/wiki/Skyrim:Captain_Metilius "Skyrim:Captain Metilius") to investigate similar sightings at [Fort Hraggstad](/wiki/Skyrim:Fort_Hraggstad "Skyrim:Fort Hraggstad"). Both versions would've also had nameless troops aid you and the designated commander.
- [Dunmer](/wiki/Skyrim:Dark_Elf "Skyrim:Dark Elf") or [Nord](/wiki/Skyrim:Nord "Skyrim:Nord") player characters will enjoy an advantage in the dragon fight, depending on whether Mirmulnir uses fire or frost attacks. If Mirmulnir uses fire breath, Dunmer characters will take only half damage due to their racial fire resistance. If Mirmulnir uses frost attacks, Nords will instead have this advantage. If Mirmulnir is using frost damage (which occurs when the player is between levels 18 and 26), the Nord guards fighting alongside the player will be more resistant to his damage, allowing them to last longer and help the player more. If Mirmulnir uses fire damage (which occurs when the player is either above level 26 or below level 18), Irileth will gain this advantage instead.
- One of the guards in the Western Watchtower mentions Hroki and Tor, two men who were stationed there before Mirmulnir apparently grabbed and ate them. Once you defeat Mirmulnir, you can find a partial Whiterun Guard's Armor set on his corpse, and it's more than likely the remains of one of them; it's unknown what happened to the other one. Coincidentally, there is a [Hroki](/wiki/Skyrim:Hroki "Skyrim:Hroki") who lives in [Markarth](/wiki/Skyrim:Markarth "Skyrim:Markarth"), though it's unlikely that Hroki would have survived, and the two are most likely unrelated, anyway.
- You can hide in the tower and let the guards take care of the dragon. Because Irileth is essential, they will always win. However, casualties will be high.
- If you have a [bow](/wiki/Skyrim:Bows "Skyrim:Bows") or [crossbow](/wiki/Skyrim:Crossbow "Skyrim:Crossbow")[DG](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard "Skyrim:Dawnguard") in your inventory, you can use Mirmulnir as target practice to improve your [Archery](/wiki/Skyrim:Archery "Skyrim:Archery") skill. Likewise, you can use [Destruction](/wiki/Skyrim:Destruction "Skyrim:Destruction") spells in the same manner.
- Once Mirmulnir is dead, other [dragons](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon "Skyrim:Dragon") will begin appearing in Skyrim, except between the end of [The Horn of Jurgen Windcaller](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Horn_of_Jurgen_Windcaller "Skyrim:The Horn of Jurgen Windcaller") and the completion of [A Blade in the Dark](/wiki/Skyrim:A_Blade_in_the_Dark "Skyrim:A Blade in the Dark").
- Before you start this quest, Western Watchtower will be an unmarked location and appear destroyed, though guards will be there, and there will be no fire.
- You don't need to wait for Balgruuf to make his speech before going to fight Mirmulnir. Right when Irileth interrupts Farengar, you can make your way to the Western Watchtower, and a quest marker will already be there.
- The Axe of Whiterun is generated in Jarl Balgruuf's inventory when you give Farengar Secret-Fire the Dragonstone. You can take a look in the Jarl's inventory and reload to generate an axe with a different enchantment. If you don't already possess one, a weapon that carries a [fire damage](/wiki/Skyrim:Fire_Damage "Skyrim:Fire Damage") effect may be especially helpful if you plan to soon proceed to the next quest in the main quest line, The Way of the Voice.
- After defeating Mirmulnir, you will be unable to fast travel directly to Dragonsreach, as its map marker will be temporarily removed. The Whiterun city gates will still be available for fast travel. However, if you open the map quickly enough, you can still fast travel to Dragonsreach.
- If you don't return to Whiterun, the Greybeards will call you if you approach High Hrothgar. After 24 hours, they will call you no matter where you are, provided you're outdoors. The main quest line will progress normally, though Dragon Rising will remain in your quest log until you speak to Balgruuf.
  - If you DO return to Whiterun immediately, the Greybeards will call you shortly after you get there.
- You must finish this quest before Message to Whiterun can be completed, regardless of who you sided with (the [Imperials](/wiki/Skyrim:Message_to_Whiterun_(Imperial) "Skyrim:Message to Whiterun (Imperial)") or the [Stormcloaks](/wiki/Skyrim:Message_to_Whiterun_(Stormcloaks) "Skyrim:Message to Whiterun (Stormcloaks)")).
- Very rarely, a guard can pull out a horn and blow it to summon reinforcements.
- Absorbing [Vulthuryol](/wiki/Skyrim:Vulthuryol "Skyrim:Vulthuryol")'s dragon soul in Blackreach will have the same effect as absorbing Mirmulnir's, if you fight Vulthuryol first.
- This quest is the only time [Whiterun Guards](/wiki/Skyrim:Whiterun_Guard "Skyrim:Whiterun Guard") will be seen wearing [hide helmets](/wiki/Skyrim:Hide_Helmet "Skyrim:Hide Helmet"), [leather helmets](/wiki/Skyrim:Leather_Helmet "Skyrim:Leather Helmet"), and [scaled helmets](/wiki/Skyrim:Scaled_Helmet "Skyrim:Scaled Helmet"), instead of their [Whiterun Guard's Helmets](/wiki/Skyrim:Whiterun_Guard%27s_Helmet "Skyrim:Whiterun Guard's Helmet"). It is also one of the few times you'll see them armed with [iron](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron "Skyrim:Iron") and/or [steel](/wiki/Skyrim:Steel "Skyrim:Steel") weaponry, instead of their standard [imperial swords](/wiki/Skyrim:Imperial_Sword "Skyrim:Imperial Sword") and [Whiterun Guard's Shields](/wiki/Skyrim:Whiterun_Guard%27s_Shield "Skyrim:Whiterun Guard's Shield"). If any die during the assault, fresh ones will replace them, potentially allowing you to collect a full set of [Whiterun Guard's Armor](/wiki/Skyrim:Whiterun_Guard%27s_Armor "Skyrim:Whiterun Guard's Armor").
- During the assault with Mirmulnir, several [burnt corpses](/wiki/Skyrim:Burnt_Corpse "Skyrim:Burnt Corpse") can be found in the courtyard east the Western Watchtower. You can loot them for gold, arrows, [bone meal](/wiki/Skyrim:Bone_Meal "Skyrim:Bone Meal"), and more.
- Mirmulnir's death is scripted to unlock the first word of [Unrelenting Force](/wiki/Skyrim:Unrelenting_Force "Skyrim:Unrelenting Force"). Killing dragons after this will allow you to collect dragon souls, though you won't be able to unlock any other shouts until you meet the Greybeards at High Hrothgar later on.
- Mirmulnir's corpse, the corpses of any fallen Whiterun Guards, and the burnt corpses will despawn from the Western Watchtower once the quest is finished, so be sure to loot them before returning to Dragonsreach.
- Version 4.3.3 of the [Unofficial Skyrim Special Edition Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Special_Edition_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Special Edition Patch") replaces the "Dohvakiin! No!!" recording with the French version.

## Bugs

- After finishing Bleak Falls Barrow by turning in the Dragonstone to Farengar, the quest Dragon Rising may fail to start.
  - This appears to be caused by Irileth being completely missing in the game. You have to first enable her through the console (`prid 0001a67f` followed by `enable`), then place her at you while you are still in Dragonsreach (`moveto player`) and finally, advance the quest (`setstage MQ104 10` then `setstage MQ104 40`). The quest rewards will be added to your inventory and Irileth will start running towards the tower.
  - If you have a save before turning the Dragonstone in to Farengar but no save from before getting the Dragonstone or simply starting the [Bleak Falls Barrow](/wiki/Skyrim:Bleak_Falls_Barrow_(quest) "Skyrim:Bleak Falls Barrow (quest)") quest, go into Dragonsreach and use the console command (`completequest MQ104`), which should advance the quest to the point of turning in the stone. You can then complete it again, and Dragon Rising should start.
- Lydia may fail to spawn properly upon completion of the quest.
  - Once you purchase Breezehome and enter it, Lydia should spawn.
- The quest reward, the Axe of Whiterun, may not appear in your inventory.
- Irileth may not always appear.
  - To fix this, wait in one hour increments and she should appear.
- With the Dragonborn add-on installed, it may be impossible to absorb the dragon soul.
  -  The [Unofficial Dragonborn Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Dragonborn_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Dragonborn Patch"), version 1.0.1, fixes this bug.
  -  This can be worked around by entering `setstage MQ104 90` into the console.
- Just as you defeat Mirmulnir, you'll see *"Dovahkiin, No!"* with subtitles enabled. However, no audio file exists for it. Similarly, you may see the following subtitles during battle: *"You are brave. Balaan hokoron. Your defeat brings me honor."*, *"Brit grah. I had forgotten what fine sport you mortals can provide!"*, or *"Thurri du hin sille ko [Sovngarde](/wiki/Skyrim:Sovngarde_(place) "Skyrim:Sovngarde (place)")!."*
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 1.2.5, fixes this bug.
- Couriers may deliver [letters](/wiki/Skyrim:Letter_from_a_Friend "Skyrim:Letter from a Friend") to find Words of Power if you use [Unrelenting Force](/wiki/Skyrim:Unrelenting_Force "Skyrim:Unrelenting Force") at the Western Watchtower.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 2.0.6, addresses this issue. The event which calls WICastMagic04 failed to check and make sure this quest was far enough along.

## Quest Stages

| Dragon Rising (MQ104) | | |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Stage | Finishes Quest | Journal Entry |
| 10 |  | I recovered the Dragonstone from Bleak Falls Barrow, as the Jarl of Whiterun requested. I should speak to him about my reward. *Objective 5:* Talk to Jarl Balgruuf |
| 13 |  | A dragon has been sighted near Whiterun. Irileth, the Jarl's housecarl, asked me to come with her to discuss the situation with Jarl Balgruuf. |
| 40 |  | A dragon has been sighted at a watchtower near Whiterun. Jarl Balgruuf has sent me along with his housecarl Irileth with reinforcements. *Objective 15:* Meet Irileth near the Western Watchtower |
| 65 |  | *Objective 20:* Kill the dragon |
| 80 |  | A dragon was sighted at a watchtower near Whiterun. Jarl Balgruuf sent me along with his housecarl Irileth with reinforcements. The dragon attacked us and we killed it. We should investigate its corpse to see if we can learn anything about where it came from. *Objective 30:* Investigate the dragon |
| 90 |  | A dragon was sighted at a watchtower near Whiterun. Jarl Balgruuf sent me along with his housecarl Irileth with reinforcements. The dragon attacked us and we killed it. When I approached the dragon's corpse, I absorbed some kind of power from it. I should return to Whiterun and tell the Jarl what happened. *Objective 40:* Report back to Jarl Balgruuf  *Objective 50:* (Optional) Use your new Shout power |
| 160 | ☑ | A dragon was sighted at a watchtower near Whiterun. Jarl Balgruuf sent me along with his housecarl Irileth with reinforcements. The dragon attacked us and we killed it. When I approached the dragon's corpse, I absorbed some kind of power from it. When I returned to Whiterun, the Jarl rewarded me for my services. I am now a Thane of Whiterun with my own personal housecarl. |

- The following empty quest stages were omitted from the table: 0, 1, 12, 15, 20, 30, 45, 46, 48, 50, 52, 55, 60, 70, 85, 92, 95, 100, 105, 108, 110, 120, 130, 150, 170, 180, 200.

Notes

- Any text displayed in angle brackets (e.g., `<Alias=LocationHold>`) is dynamically set by the Radiant Quest system, and will be filled in with the appropriate word(s) when seen in game.
- Not all Journal Entries may appear in your journal; which entries appear and which entries do not depends on the manner in which the quest is done.
- Stages are not always in order of progress. This is usually the case with quests that have multiple possible outcomes or quests where certain tasks may be done in any order. Some stages may therefore repeat objectives seen in other stages.
- If an entry is marked as "Finishes Quest" it means the quest disappears from the Active Quest list, but you may still receive new entries for that quest.
- On the PC, it is possible to use the [console](/wiki/Skyrim:Console "Skyrim:Console") to advance through the quest by entering `setstage MQ104 stage`, where `stage` is the number of the stage you wish to complete. It is not possible to un-complete (i.e. go back) quest stages, but it is possible to clear all stages of the quest using `resetquest MQ104`.

# Skyrim:Dragon's Breath Mead (quest)

## Overview

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Retrieve the [Dragon's Breath Mead](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon%27s_Breath_Mead_(item) "Skyrim:Dragon's Breath Mead (item)") and give it to either [Olda](/wiki/Skyrim:Olda "Skyrim:Olda") or [Horgeir](/wiki/Skyrim:Horgeir "Skyrim:Horgeir").** | |

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| Quest Giver: | [Olda](/wiki/Skyrim:Olda "Skyrim:Olda") |
| Location(s): | [Dragon Bridge](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Bridge "Skyrim:Dragon Bridge") |
| Reward: | Leveled gold or [Block](/wiki/Skyrim:Block "Skyrim:Block") training |
| [Disposition](/wiki/Skyrim:Disposition "Skyrim:Disposition"): | =1 ([Olda](/wiki/Skyrim:Olda "Skyrim:Olda")) =-1 ([Horgeir](/wiki/Skyrim:Horgeir "Skyrim:Horgeir")) or =-1 ([Olda](/wiki/Skyrim:Olda "Skyrim:Olda")) =1 ([Horgeir](/wiki/Skyrim:Horgeir "Skyrim:Horgeir")) |
| ID: | FreeformDragonBridge01 |

The fed-up wife

## Quick Walkthrough

1. Speak to [Olda](/wiki/Skyrim:Olda "Skyrim:Olda") in [Dragon Bridge](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Bridge "Skyrim:Dragon Bridge").
2. Find [Dragon's Breath Mead](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon%27s_Breath_Mead_(item) "Skyrim:Dragon's Breath Mead (item)").
3. Give the mead to Olda or [Horgeir](/wiki/Skyrim:Horgeir "Skyrim:Horgeir").

### The Intervention

[Olda](/wiki/Skyrim:Olda "Skyrim:Olda") lives in [Dragon Bridge](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Bridge "Skyrim:Dragon Bridge") with her husband, [Horgeir](/wiki/Skyrim:Horgeir "Skyrim:Horgeir"), who owns the local lumber mill. You will find Olda at [Horgeir's House](/wiki/Skyrim:Horgeir%27s_House "Skyrim:Horgeir's House"). If you talk to her about her husband, she will complain to you: *"He promised me, swore on his ancestors, that he'd give up the mead. And what do I find out? He's been stashing drink in a cave nearby. He even has some [wolves](/wiki/Skyrim:Wolf "Skyrim:Wolf") guarding it. I swear, I should just cut out his tongue. That would be the end of it."* If you are willing to help get her husband's stash for her, she will only ask you to bring her the bottle of [Dragon's Breath Mead](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon%27s_Breath_Mead_(item) "Skyrim:Dragon's Breath Mead (item)"), Horgeir's favorite.

The secret stash

### Dragon's Breath Mead

Take the road down the hill. Before the bridge go right, past the mill, and across the river. Head west on a rough trail and you will encounter some wolves, and possibly a bear, along the way. At the end of the trail, you will find an overhanging rock guarded by three wolves. Beneath the rock is a crate holding the Dragon's Breath Mead along with one bottle of [alto wine](/wiki/Skyrim:Alto_Wine "Skyrim:Alto Wine"), six bottles of [Nord mead](/wiki/Skyrim:Nord_Mead "Skyrim:Nord Mead") and two bottles of [wine](/wiki/Skyrim:Wine "Skyrim:Wine"). You are free to take every beverage there.

### For Your Trouble

Return to Olda and give her the mead. She will reward you with some gold, saying: *"If my Horgeir doesn't give up the mead this time, I'll hit him over the head with it."* You may instead choose to tell everything to Horgeir and return his favorite mead to him. He will regard you as a real friend and show you "how to block a punch that might be coming from some angry spouse". You will gain a one-point boost to your [Block](/wiki/Skyrim:Block "Skyrim:Block") skill. However, if you choose to help Horgeir, you will fail this quest.

## Notes

- Although it says "steal", picking up the mead does not count as stealing.
- An [iron ore vein](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron "Skyrim:Iron") is to the north of some ruins along the path.
- If you can't get Olda to initiate the quest, merely taking Horgeir's hooch from its hiding place will do so.
- Although the rest of the booze is already there, Horgeir's Dragon's Breath Mead will only spawn in the hiding location when the quest is initiated.

## Bugs

- The Dragon Breath Mead may fall through and go underneath the ground.
  - A possible fix involves using a ranged magic spell or a rune spell, such as Ice Spike, Thunderbolt, or Fire Rune to dislodge the bottle so that it can be picked up.
  - If it has fallen between the ground and wooden trough, the small space between them admits an Elven Dagger which the player can use to hit the bottle closer to the wall for retrieval. To do so, drop the dagger and grab hold of it, then move it underneath and push it toward the bottle.

## Quest Stages

| Dragon's Breath Mead (FreeformDragonBridge01) | | |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Stage | Finishes Quest | Journal Entry |
| 10 |  | *Objective 10:* Steal the Dragon's Breath Mead for Olda |
| 15 |  | *Objective 20:* Bring the Dragon's Breath Mead to Olda |

- The following empty quest stages were omitted from the table: 20, 25, 300.

Notes

- Any text displayed in angle brackets (e.g., `<Alias=LocationHold>`) is dynamically set by the Radiant Quest system, and will be filled in with the appropriate word(s) when seen in game.
- Not all Journal Entries may appear in your journal; which entries appear and which entries do not depends on the manner in which the quest is done.
- Stages are not always in order of progress. This is usually the case with quests that have multiple possible outcomes or quests where certain tasks may be done in any order. Some stages may therefore repeat objectives seen in other stages.
- If an entry is marked as "Finishes Quest" it means the quest disappears from the Active Quest list, but you may still receive new entries for that quest.
- On the PC, it is possible to use the [console](/wiki/Skyrim:Console "Skyrim:Console") to advance through the quest by entering `setstage FreeformDragonBridge01 stage`, where `stage` is the number of the stage you wish to complete. It is not possible to un-complete (i.e. go back) quest stages, but it is possible to clear all stages of the quest using `resetquest FreeformDragonBridge01`.

# Skyrim:Dragon Seekers

## Overview

| --- |
| **This page is currently being rewritten as part of the [Skyrim Quest Redesign Project](/wiki/UESPWiki:Skyrim_Quest_Redesign_Project "UESPWiki:Skyrim Quest Redesign Project").** The page is being rewritten and checked in several stages. If you make a change that is relevant to the project, please update this template accordingly, and make sure you have observed the [project guidelines](/wiki/UESPWiki:Skyrim_Quest_Redesign_Project#Guidelines "UESPWiki:Skyrim Quest Redesign Project"). [Farkas](/wiki/Skyrim:Farkas "Skyrim:Farkas") battles a dragon at [Dragontooth Crater](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragontooth_Crater "Skyrim:Dragontooth Crater").

## Quick Walkthrough

1. Speak to [Farkas](/wiki/Skyrim:Farkas "Skyrim:Farkas") or [Vilkas](/wiki/Skyrim:Vilkas "Skyrim:Vilkas") about work.
2. Travel to a [dragon lair](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Lairs "Skyrim:Dragon Lairs").
3. Kill the dragon.
4. Talk to Farkas or Vilkas.

## Detailed Walkthrough

After completing the quests [Glory of the Dead](/wiki/Skyrim:Glory_of_the_Dead "Skyrim:Glory of the Dead") and [Dragon Rising](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Rising "Skyrim:Dragon Rising"), talk to [Farkas](/wiki/Skyrim:Farkas "Skyrim:Farkas") or [Vilkas](/wiki/Skyrim:Vilkas "Skyrim:Vilkas") and tell him that you're here for work. He will tell you that he doesn't believe in dragon stories and wants to see a dragon for himself. He mentions that he heard there is a dragon at a dragon lair. The exact location can be any [dragon lair](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Lairs "Skyrim:Dragon Lairs") and will be randomly selected.

| [Eastmarch](/wiki/Skyrim:Eastmarch "Skyrim:Eastmarch") | [Falkreath Hold](/wiki/Skyrim:Falkreath_Hold "Skyrim:Falkreath Hold") | [Hjaalmarch](/wiki/Skyrim:Hjaalmarch "Skyrim:Hjaalmarch") | [The Pale](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Pale "Skyrim:The Pale") | [The Reach](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Reach "Skyrim:The Reach") | [The Rift](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Rift "Skyrim:The Rift") | [Winterhold](/wiki/Skyrim:Winterhold_(region) "Skyrim:Winterhold (region)") | [Solstheim](/wiki/Dragonborn:Solstheim "Dragonborn:Solstheim")[DB](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragonborn "Skyrim:Dragonborn") |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| [Bonestrewn Crest](/wiki/Skyrim:Bonestrewn_Crest "Skyrim:Bonestrewn Crest") | [Ancient's Ascent](/wiki/Skyrim:Ancient%27s_Ascent "Skyrim:Ancient's Ascent") | [Eldersblood Peak](/wiki/Skyrim:Eldersblood_Peak "Skyrim:Eldersblood Peak") [Skyborn Altar](/wiki/Skyrim:Skyborn_Altar "Skyrim:Skyborn Altar") | [Shearpoint](/wiki/Skyrim:Shearpoint "Skyrim:Shearpoint") | [Dragontooth Crater](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragontooth_Crater "Skyrim:Dragontooth Crater") | [Autumnwatch Tower](/wiki/Skyrim:Autumnwatch_Tower "Skyrim:Autumnwatch Tower") [Lost Tongue Overlook](/wiki/Skyrim:Lost_Tongue_Overlook "Skyrim:Lost Tongue Overlook") [Northwind Summit](/wiki/Skyrim:Northwind_Summit "Skyrim:Northwind Summit") | [Mount Anthor](/wiki/Skyrim:Mount_Anthor "Skyrim:Mount Anthor") | [Saering's Watch](/wiki/Skyrim:Saering%27s_Watch "Skyrim:Saering's Watch") |

Once you reach the predetermined dragon lair, you will find a leveled dragon. Kill the dragon and then talk to the quest-giver. He will thank you and give you a leveled sum of gold. He will then say he wants to stay for a while and honor it.

### Reward

| Levels[†](#intnote_LevelNote) | Reward[‡](#intnote_RewardBug) | USLEEP Reward |
| --- | --- | --- |
| 1–9 | 100 | 100 |
| 10–19 | 150 | 150 |
| 20–29 | 300 | 200 |
| 30–39 | 300 | 250 |
| 40+ | 300 | 300 |

[†](#note_LevelNote)Level is based on when the player completed the previous quest (or level one for the first quest), not the player's level when receiving the quest or its reward.

[‡](#note_RewardBug)The reward amounts for radiant Companions quests do not progress as intended.

-  The [Unofficial Skyrim Legendary Edition Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Legendary_Edition_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Legendary Edition Patch"), version 3.0.3, fixes this bug. ([details](https://afktrack.afkmods.com/index.php?a=issues&i=20007))

## Notes

- Farkas' and Vilkas' dialogue for this quest will express uncertainty that the rumors of the existence of dragons are true, even if they have already faced one during an earlier quest.
- You can start this quest even if you have one of [Aela the Huntress](/wiki/Skyrim:Aela_the_Huntress "Skyrim:Aela the Huntress") quests started. You can't turn in Aela's quest though until this one is finished.

## Bugs

- When reaching the lair, there may be no dragon.
  -  Setting the quest to stage 20 using the console will fix this.
- This quest may never be offered because it was listed under a story node requiring [Skjor](/wiki/Skyrim:Skjor "Skyrim:Skjor") to be alive, but he is dead by the time Glory of the Dead has begun. Completing Glory of the Dead is a requirement for this quest to be offered.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 1.2.6, fixes this bug.
  - Even if the Companions questline is finished, Skjor may be alive due to [another bug](/wiki/Skyrim:Skjor#Bugs "Skyrim:Skjor").
- Vilkas stops following you once you walk outside Jorrvaskr. The quest log indicates that the quest is completed, but the arrow on the map remains until you travel there. Once you arrive at the location of the dragon, the arrow disappears from the map, but the dragon is still there. If you don't go to the location, but instead go back inside to talk to Vilkas and activate the quest again, the quest will now show two dragons. The new one will be in the same location as the first one. The quest will claim to be complete again as soon as you step outside and Vilkas stops following again.
- If the dragon lair you are sent to is also listed in the quest log as a [Dragon bounty quest](/wiki/Skyrim:Bounty:_Dragon "Skyrim:Bounty: Dragon"), this quest does not complete once the dragon is killed. As a result, either Farkas or Vilkas cannot be dismissed as your follower and will have no dialogue options other than offering skill training. **?**
- Sometimes, despite the message 'your Companion replaces your follower' appearing, your follower may not return to their default place of residence and you will end up with both Vilkas and your current follower accompanying you. This may be beneficial to the player, and it is possible to delay completing the quest in order to keep two followers. After completing the quest, Vilkas will stay back and this will resolve itself. **?**

# Skyrim:Dragon Shouts

## Overview

Absorbing a soul from a slain dragon

**Dragon shouts** (a.k.a. **The Voice** or **Thu'um**) are phrases of [dragon language](/wiki/Lore:Dragon_Language "Lore:Dragon Language"), consisting of three separate words of power, that can be used to unleash varied powerful effects. [Dragons](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon "Skyrim:Dragon") are naturally able to use dragon shouts, but very few people possess this capability. As the [Dovahkiin](/wiki/Skyrim:Dovahkiin "Skyrim:Dovahkiin") (Dragonborn), a mortal with the soul of a dragon, you were born with this power. You can use dragon shouts only after completing [Dragon Rising](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Rising "Skyrim:Dragon Rising") in the [Main Quest](/wiki/Skyrim:Main_Quest "Skyrim:Main Quest"), from which point you can absorb a dragon's soul after slaying it. You can learn a total of 20 dragon shouts in the standard version of Skyrim, but that number can be increased to 27 dragon shouts by installing [official add-ons](/wiki/Skyrim:Add-ons "Skyrim:Add-ons").

The [Dawnguard](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard "Skyrim:Dawnguard") add-on adds three new dragon shouts for players, while [Dragonborn](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragonborn "Skyrim:Dragonborn") adds a total of four new dragon shouts.

To acquire a dragon shout, or to strengthen an existing shout:

- Discover and approach a [word wall](/wiki/Skyrim:Word_Wall "Skyrim:Word Wall") to learn a word of power.
- Unlock the word by selecting or hovering over it, and pressing **R** (PC),  (Xbox),  (Nintendo Switch) or  (PlayStation).
  - To unlock a word, you must use a dragon soul that you have absorbed. If you have no dragon souls available, you must kill a dragon and absorb its soul.
- Over the course of the main questline, you will learn 15 words of power from several characters. These words are immediately unlocked when you receive them. You will need 44 additional dragon souls to unlock all the remaining words available.

When you unlock the first word of a dragon shout, you will have access to its most basic version. Unlocking the shout's second and third words will allow for the use of a more powerful shout that will last longer, deal more damage, or have additional effects. However, certain shouts will have no effect at all unless all three words have been unlocked and are spoken at once.

## Locating Dragon Shouts

Some words of power can be learned only at certain points as you progress through the main questline. A few others require access to locations that become accessible only during specific faction quests (see the table below). Most words can be learned at any time by discovering a word wall, which are generally located at [dragon lairs](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Lairs "Skyrim:Dragon Lairs") or in [dungeons](/wiki/Skyrim:Dungeons "Skyrim:Dungeons"). There are two methods of actively seeking information on their locations, both of which can be used concurrently:

- If you use a dragon shout in towns, inhabited dungeons or encampments, a [courier](/wiki/Skyrim:Courier "Skyrim:Courier") may afterwards locate you in an outdoor area and give you a *[Letter from a Friend](/wiki/Skyrim:Letter_from_a_Friend "Skyrim:Letter from a Friend")* which will make available a miscellaneous [quest](/wiki/Skyrim:Shout_-_learn_about_word_wall "Skyrim:Shout - learn about word wall") leading to a word wall. Couriers will continue delivering such letters until all currently available words of power have been learned. However, you will not receive a new *Letter from a Friend* until you have completed the quest associated with the previous letter so received.

- Once you have completed [The Horn of Jurgen Windcaller](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Horn_of_Jurgen_Windcaller "Skyrim:The Horn of Jurgen Windcaller"), you can seek out [Arngeir](/wiki/Skyrim:Arngeir "Skyrim:Arngeir") in High Hrothgar to ask him if the Greybeards have found the locations of any words of power. He will direct you to a word wall by marking it on your map, which starts a miscellaneous [quest](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Words_of_Power "Skyrim:The Words of Power"). When you have learned all currently-available words, Arngeir will stop providing locations.

## Using Dragon Shouts

Dragon shouts are, in many ways, similar to [Magic](/wiki/Skyrim:Magic "Skyrim:Magic") but their use is not restricted by any stats or skills. To use a shout, it must first be selected from the Shouts or Favorites menu (only one shout or [Power](/wiki/Skyrim:Powers "Skyrim:Powers") can be selected at a time). The shout can then be used by pressing the [Dragon Shout/Power](/wiki/Skyrim:Controls#Power "Skyrim:Controls") button. Once the second and third words of a shout are unlocked, the shout can be "charged" by holding the shout button down. Tapping the shout button will unleash the weakest version of the shout, holding it down briefly will release the middle version, and simply holding the button will unleash the most powerful available version of the shout. Once the shout is fully charged, your character will release it automatically.

Using a shout will trigger a cool down time in which additional shouts cannot be used. The amount of time left in the cool down period can be seen as a blue outline around the compass at the top of the screen. Once the outline has receded completely, a shout can be used again. Shout cool down times vary greatly, but using more words of the shout will always make the cool down longer, with the exceptions of [Throw Voice](/wiki/Skyrim:Throw_Voice "Skyrim:Throw Voice"), [Dragon Aspect](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Aspect "Skyrim:Dragon Aspect")[DB](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragonborn "Skyrim:Dragonborn"), and [Call of Valor](/wiki/Skyrim:Call_of_Valor "Skyrim:Call of Valor"). The effects from the [Amulet of Talos](/wiki/Skyrim:Amulet_of_Talos "Skyrim:Amulet of Talos"), [Blessing of Talos](/wiki/Skyrim:Blessing_of_Talos "Skyrim:Blessing of Talos"), and [Dragon Aspect](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Aspect "Skyrim:Dragon Aspect")[DB](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragonborn "Skyrim:Dragonborn") shout reduce the cool down period and can be stacked. Meditation on a word of power with [Paarthurnax](/wiki/Skyrim:Paarthurnax_(dragon) "Skyrim:Paarthurnax (dragon)") and/or [Powers](/wiki/Skyrim:Powers#Dragonborn_Flame "Skyrim:Powers") in [Dragonborn](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragonborn "Skyrim:Dragonborn") can increase the power of certain shouts as well.

Shouts have a variety of uses both in and out of combat. Some shouts are simply helpful in traversing areas while many others can effectively turn the tide of a battle if used strategically. Since employing a powerful shout will often prevent the use of multiple shouts during a single combat, weighing a shout's effects and magnitude (one, two, or three words) versus its cool down time can help you use shouts more efficiently.

## Available Dragon Shouts

The order in which you visit word walls associated with a particular shout does not matter. Word walls will always give you the first word not already learned for a shout. This is also true of the quest-taught words of Whirlwind Sprint, learned in [The Way of the Voice](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Way_of_the_Voice "Skyrim:The Way of the Voice"), and [Fire Breath](/wiki/Skyrim:Fire_Breath "Skyrim:Fire Breath"), learned in [The Throat of the World](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Throat_of_the_World "Skyrim:The Throat of the World"); you will always learn the next word not already learned.

## Unavailable Dragon Shouts

All shouts used by dragons are different version of the ones available in the game. In addition there are a few shouts only available to certain NPCs and dragons:

- [Alduin](/wiki/Skyrim:Alduin "Skyrim:Alduin") has a dragon shout named "Dragon Storm Call". It is similar to [Storm Call](/wiki/Skyrim:Storm_Call "Skyrim:Storm Call"), but it calls forth a meteor storm instead of a lightning storm and the sky turns red instead of stormy gray. Alduin used this shout to destroy [Helgen](/wiki/Skyrim:Helgen "Skyrim:Helgen"). [Clear Skies](/wiki/Skyrim:Clear_Skies "Skyrim:Clear Skies") interrupts the storm.
- Alduin has another shout called "ResurrectionShout" that resurrects dead dragons. Its words of power are "Slen Tiid Vo", which translate to "Flesh Time (Opposite of)". It should be noted that you can learn the words Tiid (Time) and Slen (Flesh), showing that words can be part of different shouts.
- The soul-snare mist created by Alduin in [Sovngarde](/wiki/Skyrim:Sovngarde_(place) "Skyrim:Sovngarde (place)") is technically not a dragon shout, but a script. It creates a mist where Alduin hides and feeds upon the trapped souls. Its words of power are "Ven Mul Riik", which translate to "Wind Strong Gale".
- The shout used by [Tsun](/wiki/Skyrim:Tsun "Skyrim:Tsun") to return you to [Nirn](/wiki/Lore:Nirn "Lore:Nirn") from Sovngarde is another unavailable shout. Its words of power are "Nahl Daal Vus", which translate to "Living Return Nirn".
- The shout used by the Greybeards to create ethereal forms for you to practice shouts on is called [Phantom Form‎](/wiki/Skyrim:Phantom_Form "Skyrim:Phantom Form"). Its words of power are "Fiik Lo Sah", which is translated as "Mirror Deceive Phantom". The shout was apparently intended to be available, as it is voiced for all races.
- During the learning of Whirlwind Sprint, [Borri](/wiki/Skyrim:Borri "Skyrim:Borri") opens the gate doors by saying "Bex", meaning "Open". This is not a shout, but a script.
- [Dwarven Centurions](/wiki/Skyrim:Dwarven_Centurion "Skyrim:Dwarven Centurion") have a "Steam Breath" power that is treated as a dragon shout by the game engine. The closest thing you can obtain to this is the lesser power [Breath of Nchuak](/wiki/Skyrim:Breath_of_Nchuak "Skyrim:Breath of Nchuak"), added by [Dragonborn](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragonborn "Skyrim:Dragonborn") and only available with the [Visage of Mzund](/wiki/Skyrim:Visage_of_Mzund "Skyrim:Visage of Mzund") equipped.
- [Dawnguard](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard "Skyrim:Dawnguard") adds [Soul Cairn Summon](/wiki/Skyrim:Soul_Cairn_Summon "Skyrim:Soul Cairn Summon"), a shout unique to [Durnehviir](/wiki/Skyrim:Durnehviir_(dragon) "Skyrim:Durnehviir (dragon)"). Its words of power are "Diil Qoth Zaam", translated as "Undead Tomb Slave". Each word summons an undead minion from the Soul Cairn; the full shout will summon a [wrathman](/wiki/Skyrim:Wrathman "Skyrim:Wrathman"), [boneman](/wiki/Skyrim:Boneman "Skyrim:Boneman"), and [mistman](/wiki/Skyrim:Mistman "Skyrim:Mistman") to aid Durnehviir in combat. These summons are available to you, but rather in spell form. Even if you obtain this shout with [console](/wiki/Skyrim:Console "Skyrim:Console") commands, you can only summon one undead unless you use the console to add the multiple summon perk that Durnehviir has.

## Notes

- You can absorb one dragon soul without fighting a dragon after finishing the quest [The Horn of Jurgen Windcaller](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Horn_of_Jurgen_Windcaller "Skyrim:The Horn of Jurgen Windcaller").
- The souls [Miraak](/wiki/Skyrim:Miraak_(person) "Skyrim:Miraak (person)")[DB](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragonborn "Skyrim:Dragonborn") stole from you throughout the game will be returned when you kill him during the quest [At the Summit of Apocrypha](/wiki/Skyrim:At_the_Summit_of_Apocrypha "Skyrim:At the Summit of Apocrypha").
- If you use a dragon shout in a city while there are no hostile opponents present, a guard may run up to you and ask you to stop, complaining that the villagers are getting nervous; however, there are no other consequences, regardless of the dialogue option chosen or whether you continue to shout.
  - This is true even for shouts that are not supposed to reveal your location to others, such as Aura Whisper or Throw Voice, or for shouts that have no effect, such as Elemental Fury without an equipped weapon.
- The three race categories (Human, Mer, and Beast) have their own unique voices and pronunciations when shouting.[*verification needed — see [talk page](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Skyrim_talk:Dragon_Shouts)*]
- The male human shouts (Breton, Nord, Imperial, and Redguard) were voiced by Mark Lampert, the game's sound designer.
- The following NPCs are able to use dragon shouts: all members of the [Greybeards](/wiki/Skyrim:Greybeards "Skyrim:Greybeards"), [Ulfric Stormcloak](/wiki/Skyrim:Ulfric_Stormcloak "Skyrim:Ulfric Stormcloak"), [Felldir the Old](/wiki/Skyrim:Felldir_the_Old "Skyrim:Felldir the Old"), [Gormlaith Golden-Hilt](/wiki/Skyrim:Gormlaith_Golden-Hilt "Skyrim:Gormlaith Golden-Hilt"), [Hakon One-Eye](/wiki/Skyrim:Hakon_One-Eye "Skyrim:Hakon One-Eye"), [Tsun](/wiki/Skyrim:Tsun "Skyrim:Tsun"), the [Ebony Warrior](/wiki/Skyrim:Ebony_Warrior "Skyrim:Ebony Warrior")[DB](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragonborn "Skyrim:Dragonborn"), and [Miraak](/wiki/Skyrim:Miraak_(person) "Skyrim:Miraak (person)")[DB](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragonborn "Skyrim:Dragonborn").
- All dragons, some draugr and draugr deathlords can also use the Voice.
- When the Greybeards teach Whirlwind Sprint to you, after you learn the word but before they give you the power to use it, you can use a dragon soul to unlock it. Afterwards, the Greybeards will gift you with the power to use it, therefore giving you two words of Whirlwind Sprint. (This also works when [Paarthurnax](/wiki/Skyrim:Paarthurnax_(dragon) "Skyrim:Paarthurnax (dragon)") teaches you Fire Breath.)
  - If you do this, then reading a second word will not grant you the third word. You will still have to read all three words to learn all three words.

## Bugs

- Arngeir may not give you the option to ask him for words of power.
- Sometimes, the word will not appear on the wall, leaving you unable to learn the entire shout. There does not appear to be a fix for this; even loading from a previous save will not cause the word to appear. Associated audio and visual effects may be present, but you will not learn the word. The audio will continue to play every time you visit the site. It is possible that the word will become available at the wall if the area is left unvisited for a long period of time.
  -  One fix is using the console command `player.teachword wordid` -- however, this will not finish related quests. For the `teachword` command, you need the id of each shout's individual word of power, not the id posted in the table here, and they can be found on each shout's individual page.
    -  Using the command `SetStage FreeFormHighHrothgarA 20` will end [The Words of Power](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Words_of_Power "Skyrim:The Words of Power") and allow you to acquire another quest normally. This only ends the quest; you will still need to use the `teachword` command to learn the shout.
- Some of the sound files do not match the words of some shouts. For example, the female Khajiit voicing for "Marked For Death" is only "Krii!" for the single tap version (one word) - the 3 word version comes out "Yun Lud Aus!" instead.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 2.0.0, fixes this bug.
- Sometimes when you kill a dragon, it will die and its body will be lootable, but you will not absorb its soul. This is usually the result of a dragon you already killed earlier respawning.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 1.0, fixes this bug.
- If a shout is activated while in the water where you can't use it, then it will activate as soon as you would be able to (as soon as the water becomes shallow); however, no matter what words of the shout you know or how long you hold it, it will always cast the weakest version.
- If a shout is activated while holding a drawn bow, then it will activate as soon as you would be able to (once you're finished sheathing/firing your bow); however, no matter what words of the shout you know or how long you hold it, it will always cast the weakest version. **?**
- The first word of clear skies, "Lok", sounds the same regardless of race or gender. **?**
- Using the soul of a dragon to unlock a shout while the animation for the soul absorption is still playing will grant you another soul after the "dragon soul absorbed" message appears. **?**
- With [Dawnguard](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard "Skyrim:Dawnguard") installed, dragon souls may not unlock new shouts, even if the player has more than one dragon soul. **?**

## Achievements

[Achievements](/wiki/Skyrim:Achievements "Skyrim:Achievements") related to dragon shouts are listed below.

-  **Dragon Soul** (10 points/Bronze) — Absorb a [dragon](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon "Skyrim:Dragon") soul
  - This achievement is unlocked during [Dragon Rising](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Rising "Skyrim:Dragon Rising"), since it is the first quest where a dragon can be killed.
-  **Dragonrider**[DB](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragonborn "Skyrim:Dragonborn") (20 points/Bronze) — Tame and ride 5 [dragons](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon "Skyrim:Dragon")
-  **Dragon Aspect**[DB](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragonborn "Skyrim:Dragonborn") (20 points/Silver) — Learn all 3 words of [Dragon Aspect](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Aspect "Skyrim:Dragon Aspect")
-  **Dragon Hunter** (20 points/Bronze) — Absorb 20 dragon souls
  - Any twenty dragons can be killed to obtain this achievement.
  - You can track your progress towards this achievement using the "Dragon Souls Collected" statistic, on the "Magic" page of your journal's "General Stats" section.
-  **Words of Power** (10 points/Bronze) — Learn all three words of a shout
  - Most players will unlock this achievement at the end of [The Horn of Jurgen Windcaller](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Horn_of_Jurgen_Windcaller "Skyrim:The Horn of Jurgen Windcaller"), when the final word of [Unrelenting Force](/wiki/Skyrim:Unrelenting_Force "Skyrim:Unrelenting Force") is learned from the [Greybeards](/wiki/Skyrim:Greybeards "Skyrim:Greybeards"). However, it can also be unlocked by visiting all three word walls for any given dragon shout. [Shearpoint](/wiki/Skyrim:Shearpoint "Skyrim:Shearpoint") has all three words of the [Throw Voice](/wiki/Skyrim:Throw_Voice "Skyrim:Throw Voice") shout.
-  **Thu'um Master** (40 points/Silver) — Learn 20 shouts
  - To unlock this achievement, one word of each of the twenty available shouts must be unlocked (learning any twenty different words of power is not sufficient).
  - It cannot be unlocked until the [main quest](/wiki/Skyrim:Main_Quest "Skyrim:Main Quest") is completed, because several of the shouts are only learned as part of the main quest — and one shout ([Call of Valor](/wiki/Skyrim:Call_of_Valor "Skyrim:Call of Valor")) is only learned at the completion of the final quest, [Dragonslayer](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragonslayer "Skyrim:Dragonslayer"). This is no longer the case with the release of the add-ons as other shouts are now available.
  - The other shout that is easy to miss for this achievement is [Throw Voice](/wiki/Skyrim:Throw_Voice "Skyrim:Throw Voice"), since it can only be learned in one location, Shearpoint.
  - You can track your progress towards this achievement using the "Shouts Learned" statistic, on the "Magic" page of your journal's "General Stats" section.
-  **Soul Tear**[DG](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard "Skyrim:Dawnguard") (20 points/Bronze) — Learn all three words of [Soul Tear](/wiki/Skyrim:Soul_Tear "Skyrim:Soul Tear")
